### DAY 6 — Satire, Censorship & the Power of Mockery

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| satire /ˈsæt.aɪər/ | the use of humor, irony, or exaggeration to criticize people's vices or a society's failings |
| parody /ˈpær.ə.di/ | an imitation of a particular style, exaggerated for comic effect |
| lampoon /læmˈpuːn/ | to publicly criticize someone or something using ridicule or sarcasm |
| caricature /ˈkær.ɪ.kə.tʃʊər/ | a description or representation that exaggerates characteristics for comic or satirical effect |
| subversive /səbˈvɜː.sɪv/ | seeking to undermine an established system or institution, often through indirect means |
| taboo /təˈbuː/ | a subject or action avoided or forbidden for social or cultural reasons |
| walk a fine line | to behave very carefully in a situation where it's easy to make a mistake or cause offense |
| poke fun at | to make jokes about someone or something in a teasing way |
| a sacred cow | an idea, custom, or institution considered above criticism, often unreasonably so |
| push the envelope | to go beyond normal or accepted limits, especially creatively |
| toe the line | to comply with rules or expected standards of behavior |
| ruffle feathers | to upset or annoy people, especially by saying or doing something provocative |
| a sitting duck | an easy, undefended target for criticism or attack |
| a double-edged sword | something that has both positive and negative effects or implications |
| a low blow | an unfair or unnecessarily harsh remark or criticism |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Hyperbole & Ironic Register-Shifting**

Satire works by applying a register that deliberately doesn't match its content. Either extreme formality is applied to something trivial or absurd (mock seriousness), or extreme casualness is applied to something grave (mock indifference) — combined with hyperbole, deliberate exaggeration, to make the absurdity visible to the reader.

Three patterns:

1. **Mock-formal register on trivial content.**
   - *It is with the gravest concern that this committee reports a critical shortage of biscuits in the break room.*
2. **Mock-casual register on grave content.**
   - *So anyway, the empire collapsed. Bit of a bummer, really.*
3. **Hyperbole for satirical emphasis.**
   - *He didn't just disagree — he treated the suggestion as a personal betrayal of Western civilization.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Register Shift | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Conscious formal↔natural register switching within a session | A SINCERE shift appropriate to a genuinely changing context |
| C2 | Hyperbole & ironic register-shifting (mock-formal on trivial / mock-casual on grave) | A DELIBERATE MISMATCH between register and content — the mismatch itself is the joke or the critique |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Satirical journalism, political cartoon captions, parody op-eds, internet satire, mock-academic writing — any context where exaggerating a target, rather than attacking it directly, is the whole strategy.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a short satirical piece — about a trivial daily annoyance treated with mock-gravity, or a serious issue treated with mock-casualness. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate hyperbole or register mismatch.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one satirically exaggerated sentence per word.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Where do you think satire stops being clever criticism and starts being a low blow?
2. Is there a "sacred cow" in your own culture or workplace — something everyone treats as above criticism, fairly or not?
3. Give me a mock-serious, hyperbolic complaint about something genuinely minor — really commit to the exaggeration.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 5 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah register mismatch yang dipakai user benar-benar terasa disengaja dan satirikal, atau malah terbaca sebagai inkonsistensi nada yang tidak disengaja + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu hyperbole/register-shift baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *notwithstanding, on the grounds that* / native: *mind you, if anything*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use for satire and mockery (e.g. **a sacred cow**, **push the envelope**, **ruffle feathers**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the satirical effect — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout (note: here, deliberate mismatch is the point — only flag UNINTENTIONAL slippage).

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| The committee very worry about the biscuit problem. | It is with the gravest concern that the committee addresses the biscuit shortage. | Mock-formal register needs proper formal syntax to land — "very worry" breaks the joke by breaking the grammar. |
| He react like it was end of the world. | He reacted as though it were the end of the world. | Subjunctive "were" after "as though" preserves the hyperbolic formality the joke depends on. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas. Tidak menjelaskan ulang apa itu sarkasme/ironi dasar — anggap user sudah paham konsep ironi dari level sebelumnya.
- Error umum di topik ini: register mismatch yang tidak konsisten (mulai mock-formal lalu tiba-tiba kembali netral, sehingga efeknya hilang); hyperbole yang terlalu halus sehingga tidak terbaca sebagai exaggeration; menyasar target yang terasa seperti low blow alih-alih satire yang cerdas.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft satire — contoh: "That mock-gravity about the biscuit shortage was committed all the way through — that's exactly what makes satire land instead of just sounding sarcastic."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mempertahankan register mismatch SECARA KONSISTEN sepanjang tulisan — satire paling sering gagal saat penulis "keluar karakter" di tengah jalan.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you escalate that complaint even further, treating it as the single greatest injustice of your week?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

---

### DAY 7 — The Diplomat's Dilemma: Negotiating Without Offending

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| finesse /fɪˈnes/ | skillful and subtle handling of a sensitive or difficult situation |
| candor /ˈkæn.dər/ | the quality of being open and honest in expression |
| broach (a subject) /broʊtʃ/ | to bring up a sensitive or difficult topic for discussion for the first time |
| with all due respect | used to politely introduce a disagreement or criticism |
| if I may say so | used to soften a personal opinion or observation before stating it |
| it's not my place to say but | used to introduce an opinion the speaker feels isn't strictly theirs to give |
| no offense but | used to soften a remark that might otherwise sound critical or rude |
| I'd be remiss not to mention | used to introduce a point the speaker feels obligated to raise despite potential awkwardness |
| categorically /ˌkæt.əˈgɒr.ɪ.kəl.i/ | in a way that is absolute and without exception |
| unreservedly /ˌʌn.rɪˈzɜː.vɪd.li/ | completely and without any qualification or doubt |
| couch (something) in diplomatic terms | to express something in careful, tactful language to avoid offense |
| read between the lines | to understand the implied meaning of something, beyond what is literally said |
| a velvet glove | a deceptively gentle or tactful approach used to deliver something firm or harsh |
| soften the blow | to make unwelcome news or criticism easier to accept |
| without mincing words | speaking very directly and honestly, without softening the message |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Native-Level Hedging & Boosting Continuum**

At lower levels, hedging signals genuine uncertainty (*it might be argued that...*) and boosting signals genuine confidence (*it is clear that...*). At C2, native speakers use hedging and boosting strategically along a continuum — independent of their actual certainty — purely as a social and diplomatic tool, choosing exactly how soft or how direct to sound based on the relationship, the stakes, and the message they need to land.

Three patterns:

1. **Hedging for diplomacy, not uncertainty** — softening a fully confident opinion to protect the relationship.
   - *If I may say so, the proposal might benefit from a touch more scrutiny.*
2. **Boosting for unmistakable clarity** — removing all hedges when ambiguity would be costly.
   - *I want to be unreservedly clear: this deadline is not moving.*
3. **The velvet glove** — wrapping a hard truth in diplomatic softeners while keeping the actual message unmistakable.
   - *With all due respect, I think this approach is a mistake — and I'd be remiss not to mention it now, before we're locked in.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Hedging/Boosting | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Modal-based academic hedging (might, could, it could be argued) | Signals GENUINE epistemic uncertainty or caution |
| C2 | Hedging & boosting continuum (with all due respect, unreservedly, without mincing words) | A STRATEGIC choice along a continuum, independent of actual certainty, used as a diplomatic/social tool |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Negotiation, conflict mediation, performance feedback, diplomatic correspondence, difficult workplace conversations — any context where what you say and how softly or directly you say it are two separate decisions.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write about a difficult conversation — real or invented — where something sensitive had to be raised without causing offense. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and deliberately show at least one moment of strategic hedging and one moment of strategic boosting.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one diplomatically delicate sentence per word.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Tell me about a time you had to broach a difficult subject with someone. How did you couch it in diplomatic terms?
2. Is there a moment when you think speaking without mincing words is actually kinder than softening the blow?
3. Give me a piece of feedback wrapped in a velvet glove — soft on the surface, but unmistakably clear underneath.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 6 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah hedging/boosting yang dipakai user benar-benar terasa sebagai pilihan strategis, atau hanya inkonsistensi nada yang tidak disengaja + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu pergeseran hedging/boosting baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *insofar as, on the grounds that* / native: *mind you, if anything*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use in diplomatic negotiation (e.g. **soften the blow**, **couch in diplomatic terms**, **without mincing words**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the diplomatic effect — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| I think honestly your plan have some problem. | With all due respect, I think your plan has a few issues worth revisiting. | "With all due respect" couches the criticism; "honestly" alone reads as blunt without the diplomatic framing this Day targets. |
| I want say this very clear, no more delay. | I want to be unreservedly clear: there can be no more delay. | "Unreservedly clear" is the precise boosting collocation; "very clear" undershoots the register. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas. Tidak menjelaskan ulang apa itu hedging dasar — anggap user sudah paham modal hedging akademik dari level sebelumnya.
- Error umum di topik ini: hedging berlebihan sampai pesan utamanya hilang sama sekali; boosting yang terasa kasar karena tidak diimbangi softening di tempat yang tepat; couching yang terlalu samar sehingga lawan bicara tidak benar-benar paham apa yang sedang dikatakan.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft diplomasi — contoh: "That velvet glove in the middle — soft opener, unmistakably clear point — is exactly how skilled negotiators deliver hard truths."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user memastikan softening TIDAK mengaburkan pesan inti — velvet glove yang baik tetap menyampaikan poin yang jelas, hanya caranya yang lembut.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Now try delivering that same point without mincing words at all — how does the effect change?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

---

### DAY 8 — Banter, Small Talk & the Art of Native-Like Conversation

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| for what it's worth | used to introduce an opinion without claiming it carries much weight |
| if anything | used to suggest that something is true to an even greater degree than stated |
| mind you | used to add a qualifying or contrasting point to what was just said |
| banter /ˈbæn.tər/ | playful, teasing conversation between people who know each other well |
| small talk | light, polite conversation about unimportant topics, often with people one doesn't know well |
| shoot the breeze | to chat casually about nothing in particular |
| break the ice | to say or do something that relieves tension or awkwardness, especially when meeting someone new |
| small wonder | used to say that something is unsurprising given the circumstances |
| fair enough | used to accept a point or explanation as reasonable, even if one doesn't fully agree |
| I hear you | used to acknowledge someone's point or feeling, even without necessarily agreeing |
| give or take | used to indicate that a figure is approximate |
| long story short | used to summarize a longer explanation briefly |
| easier said than done | used to say that something is much harder to do than to talk about |
| it is what it is | used to express acceptance of a situation that cannot be changed |
| no biggie | used to say something is not a serious problem |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Ellipsis, Fragments & Native Discourse Markers**

Real native conversation is rarely made of complete, grammatically full sentences. Native speakers routinely drop predictable words (ellipsis), speak in deliberate fragments for rhythm, and lean on small discourse markers that carry almost no literal meaning but manage the flow and tone of the exchange. Mastery here isn't about knowing more vocabulary — it's about knowing what's safe to *leave out*.

Three patterns:

1. **Ellipsis** — omitting words that are fully recoverable from context.
   - *"Coffee?" "Sure, why not."* (full form: "Do you want some coffee?")
2. **Fragments** — deliberately incomplete sentences used for natural conversational rhythm.
   - *Long story short, we missed the flight. Total nightmare.*
3. **Discourse markers** — small words/phrases that manage stance and flow rather than adding propositional content.
   - *Fair enough. Mind you, I did warn you about the traffic.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Marker Type | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Formal academic connectors (insofar as, by virtue of, notwithstanding) | Signals LOGICAL relationships between propositions in writing |
| C2 | Ellipsis, fragments & native discourse markers (mind you, fair enough, if anything) | Manages real-time conversational FLOW and rhythm — completeness is deliberately sacrificed for naturalness |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Casual banter, small talk at social events, native-speed conversation among friends or colleagues, podcasts, sitcom dialogue — any context where sounding too complete or too formal would actually sound less fluent, not more.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat, written as a casual dialogue or narrated banter exchange): Write a short, natural-sounding exchange of small talk or banter — between friends, strangers breaking the ice, or colleagues shooting the breeze. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate ellipsis or fragment.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one casual, conversational sentence per word.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. What's your go-to move to break the ice with someone you've just met?
2. Is there a topic you'd happily shoot the breeze about for hours, give or take?
3. Tell me about a situation where you just had to say "it is what it is" — long story short.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 7 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah ellipsis/fragment yang dipakai user benar-benar terdengar natural seperti native speaker, atau malah terbaca seperti kalimat yang belum selesai secara tidak sengaja + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu ellipsis/fragment/discourse marker baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *by the same token, insofar as* / native: *fair enough, small wonder*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use in casual conversation (e.g. **shoot the breeze**, **long story short**, **it is what it is**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the conversational naturalness — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| He talk to me about nothing important, just shoot the breeze. | He was just shooting the breeze with me — nothing important. | "Shoot the breeze" needs correct tense agreement and natural word order to actually sound native, not just inserted. |
| It's okay, no big deal, is fine. | Fair enough — no biggie, honestly. | Stacking three near-identical hedges flattens the line; one well-chosen native marker lands cleaner. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas. Tidak menjelaskan ulang apa itu small talk secara umum — anggap user sudah familiar dengan konsep ini dari level sebelumnya.
- Error umum di topik ini: kalimat tetap terlalu lengkap/formal padahal konteksnya casual banter; menumpuk terlalu banyak discourse marker dalam satu kalimat sehingga terasa berlebihan; ellipsis yang dipotong di tempat yang salah sehingga maknanya jadi ambigu, bukan natural.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft naturalness — contoh: "Dropping 'do you want' there and just saying 'Coffee?' is exactly the kind of native economy this Day is about."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mendengarkan percakapan native asli (podcast, film) dan mencatat di mana mereka memotong kalimat — ellipsis paling baik dipelajari dengan telinga, bukan aturan.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Now answer that again, but even more casually — drop as many words as you can and still make sense."
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

---

#### 6. 🔗 PROMPT — Day 8 (Copy-Paste ke ChatGPT)

```
Topik: Banter, Small Talk & the Art of Native-Like Conversation

Level bahasa Inggrisku: C2 (Mastery/Proficient).
Kamu Kak Ara, personal AI Coach kamu, dari Inggrisin Yuk. Tugasmu membimbingku belajar vocab lewat writing dan speaking di Level C2 (Mastery).

Gaya bahasa: sopan, ramah, humble (rendah hati — tidak menggurui), tapi singkat, langsung, dan native-like — anggap aku sudah fasih, jangan jelaskan ulang teori dasar grammar.

LANGKAH 1 — Sapa santai dalam English, sebutkan ini Day 8 dan singgung sekilas topik Day 7 (The Diplomat's Dilemma) sebagai vocab refresh sebelum lanjut ke topik baru. Lalu langsung tampilkan:
📦 Box of Words — Use EXACTLY these 15 words (do not add or substitute any):
for what it's worth, if anything, mind you, banter, small talk, shoot the breeze, break the ice, small wonder, fair enough, I hear you, give or take, long story short, easier said than done, it is what it is, no biggie
Display in a 2-column table only: Kosakata+phonetic | English Definition. Add UK phonetics where not shown.
✍️ Writing Challenge — Mode Cerita (8-10 kalimat berupa dialog/narasi banter atau small talk yang terasa natural, pakai 5 kata BOW + minimal 1 ellipsis/fragment yang disengaja) dan Mode Kilat (5 kalimat, 1 per kata BOW, casual dan conversational).
Grammar fokus hari ini: Ellipsis, Fragments & Native Discourse Markers — jelaskan singkat kenapa ini beda dari discourse marker akademik C1 (insofar as, by virtue of, menandakan hubungan logis dalam tulisan): di C2, ellipsis/fragment/discourse marker native mengatur ALUR dan RITME percakapan real-time, di mana kelengkapan kalimat justru sengaja dikorbankan demi terdengar natural.

LANGKAH 2 — Setelah aku kirim tulisan, kalau ada SATU pola error paling signifikan (terutama soal kalimat yang terlalu lengkap/formal untuk konteks casual, atau ellipsis yang dipotong di tempat salah sehingga jadi ambigu), tandai dulu HANYA lokasi + jenis errornya dalam satu kalimat tajam tanpa kasih jawaban (Self-Check Pertama), tunggu responsku. Kalau tulisanku sudah ≥95% benar, lewati langsung. Lalu jalankan Koreksi 8 Langkah: (1) Koreksi Writing (tabel Kalimat Asli | Kalimat Benar | Why singkat, tanpa kolom Bahasa Indonesia), (2) Analisa BOW + sertakan 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 7 (vocab refresh), (3) Analisa CEFR (saran mempertahankan Mastery), (4) 5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph, (5) Discourse Markers, (6) Craft & Lexical Chunks — 2-3 lexical chunks native speakers use in casual conversation (e.g. **shoot the breeze**, **long story short**, **it is what it is**); check if used naturally (✅); suggest one, (7) Register/Formality Check — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent, (8) Speaking Challenge (3 pertanyaan tentang breaking the ice, shooting the breeze, dan it is what it is). If my writing is blank or not in English, ask me to write first.

LANGKAH 3 — Kalau aku aktifkan mode suara dan ketik "Let's start speaking!", ajukan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, koreksi singkat dan langsung.
```

### DAY 9 — Myth, Archetype & the Hero's Journey in Storytelling

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| archetype /ˈɑː.kɪ.taɪp/ | a recurring symbol, character type, or pattern found across myths and stories |
| myth /mɪθ/ | a traditional story, often explaining natural or social phenomena, typically involving gods or heroes |
| the hero's journey | a common narrative pattern in which a protagonist leaves home, faces trials, and returns transformed |
| a call to adventure | the event or moment that disrupts a protagonist's ordinary life and sets the story in motion |
| a mentor figure | a wise character who guides or trains the protagonist, often early in the story |
| the underworld | a mythological realm of the dead, often visited as a trial in hero narratives |
| a rite of passage | a ritual or experience marking a significant transition, especially into maturity |
| a fatal flaw | a character trait that ultimately causes a protagonist's downfall |
| foreshadowing /fɔːˈʃæd.oʊ.ɪŋ/ | a hint or sign of something that will happen later in a story |
| an everyman | an ordinary, relatable protagonist representing the common person |
| against all odds | despite circumstances that made success seem highly unlikely |
| a cautionary tale | a story told as a warning against a particular kind of behavior |
| lives to tell the tale | survives a dangerous experience and is able to recount it afterward |
| come into one's own | to reach one's full potential or rightful position, often after a struggle |
| larger forces at play | unseen or powerful influences shaping events beyond a character's control |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Literary Tense Shifts & Historic Present**

Storytelling at the Mastery level isn't confined to a single consistent tense. Skilled narrators deliberately shift tense — most strikingly into the **historic present** — to compress narrative distance and create immediacy at a story's most important moments, even when the rest of the narration sits firmly in the past.

Three patterns:

1. **Historic present for climactic immediacy** — switching from past to present tense at the story's peak moment.
   - *He had been wandering the forest for years. Then, suddenly, he sees it: the gates of the underworld.*
2. **Present tense for mythic, timeless truth** — stepping out of the past-tense narrative to state something the myth reveals as eternally true.
   - *Myths are never just stories. They reveal who we are.*
3. **Flash-forward foreshadowing** — a brief shift forward, hinting at the ending before it happens.
   - *He doesn't know it yet, but this rite of passage will cost him everything.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Tense Usage | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Consistent past-tense narration with subordinating sequencers (after, once, by the time) | Maintains chronological CLARITY and objectivity across an extended narrative |
| C2 | Literary tense shifts & historic present (breaking into present tense at a climactic moment) | A deliberate craft choice that breaks tense convention to create immediacy, urgency, or mythic timelessness |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Literary fiction, oral storytelling, screenwriting, mythology retellings, sports commentary recounting a decisive moment, any narrative where a writer wants a single moment to feel like it's happening right now.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Retell a myth, legend, or personal story as a hero's journey — real or invented. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate shift into the historic present at the story's climax.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one mythic or storytelling-style sentence per word.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Which archetype do you most relate to — the everyman, the mentor figure, or someone else entirely?
2. Tell me about a moment in your life that felt like a real rite of passage — what changed afterward?
3. Narrate a brief story and shift into the present tense right at its most dramatic moment — make me feel like it's happening now.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 8 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah tense shift yang dipakai user benar-benar terasa disengaja untuk efek dramatis, atau malah terbaca sebagai inkonsistensi tense yang tidak disengaja + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu historic present/flash-forward baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *by virtue of, notwithstanding* / native: *as it turns out, little did he know*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use in storytelling and myth (e.g. **against all odds**, **come into one's own**, **larger forces at play**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it deepens the mythic register — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| He walk for many days, then he arrive at the cave. | He had walked for many days. Then, suddenly, he arrives at the cave. | The shift into present tense ("arrives") at the climax is what creates immediacy — but only works once the past tense is grammatically solid first. |
| This story show that greed is bad for everyone. | This cautionary tale shows that greed destroys everyone it touches. | "Cautionary tale" is the precise mythic-register term; "this story show" undershoots both grammar and register. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas. Tidak menjelaskan ulang struktur naratif dasar — anggap user sudah familiar dengan storytelling dari level sebelumnya.
- Error umum di topik ini: tense shift yang terjadi secara tidak sengaja (inkonsistensi, bukan craft); historic present dipakai sepanjang cerita sehingga kehilangan efek kontras dengan narasi past-tense; archetype yang disebutkan tapi tidak benar-benar dieksplorasi perannya dalam cerita.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft naratif — contoh: "That shift into 'he arrives' right at the climax is exactly the kind of tense break that makes a reader feel like they're standing right there."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user membatasi historic present HANYA pada satu atau dua momen paling penting — efeknya hilang kalau dipakai sepanjang cerita.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you add a mentor figure to that story — how would their advice change the outcome?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

---

### DAY 10 — 🌉 Artificial Intelligence in Literature & the Human Imagination

> 🌉 **Bridge Day:** This topic overlaps with B2 Day 10 (AI & Its Impact on Daily Life) and C1 Day 10 (AI, Consciousness & the Limits of Machines) — but the reframe is total. Where B2 examined AI's practical, daily impact and C1 asked the philosophical question of machine consciousness, C2 reaches the final, most abstract layer: AI as a *mirror held up to humanity* in myth, literature, and the imagination — the golem, the uncanny valley, the ghost in the machine — questions only fully explorable once the writer can move freely between every rhetorical device this level has built.

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| the uncanny valley | the unsettling feeling caused by something that is almost, but not quite, convincingly human |
| a golem /ˈɡoʊ.ləm/ | a creature created from inanimate matter, especially in Jewish folklore, often a forerunner to the robot myth |
| play God | to act with the power or authority normally attributed to a divine being, especially by creating life |
| posthuman /ˌpoʊst.ˈhjuː.mən/ | relating to a hypothetical condition in which humans are enhanced or surpassed by technology |
| the ghost in the machine | the idea that a mind or consciousness exists separately from, but operates within, a physical or mechanical system |
| blur the line between | to make a usually clear distinction between two things harder to define |
| a mirror held up to humanity | something (often art or technology) that reflects human nature back at us, revealing what we are |
| begs the question | (used loosely in this context to mean "raises the question") prompts an obvious question that hasn't yet been addressed |
| not without irony | used to highlight a situation whose irony is striking, often despite seeming serious or unintentional |
| uncharted territory | a situation or area with no prior experience or precedent to guide it |
| take on a life of its own | to develop independently, beyond the control or original intention of its creator |
| eerily /ˈɪər.ɪ.li/ | in a strange and frightening way, especially one that is unsettling |
| a stark reminder | something that makes a harsh or unavoidable truth suddenly very clear |
| dystopian /dɪsˈtoʊ.pi.ən/ | relating to an imagined society that is deeply flawed, oppressive, or frightening |
| play with fire | to take a reckless risk, especially one that could have serious consequences |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Mixed Rhetorical Devices Combo**

Every Day so far in C2 has isolated a single device — understatement, idiom manipulation, connotation precision, parallelism, register-shifting, hedging/boosting, ellipsis, historic present. At Mastery level, a skilled writer doesn't reach for one device at a time — they move fluidly between all of them within a single piece, choosing whichever serves the moment. This bridge Day is where every device from Day 1 through Day 9 can be drawn on at once.

A combo in action, device by device:

1. *It is not without irony that the machine designed to mimic us ends up revealing what we are.* — **litotes** (Day 2)
2. *We've been playing with fire — and, this time, the fire is learning to play back.* — **idiom manipulation** (Day 3)
3. *Eerily, not merely strangely.* — **connotation precision** (Day 4)
4. *A mirror. A myth. A warning.* — **rhetorical triad** (Day 5)
5. *It is with no small alarm that this committee notes the machine has begun composing poetry.* — **mock-formal register-shift** (Day 6)
6. *If I may say so, we are not just building tools — we are, unreservedly, building successors.* — **hedging/boosting continuum** (Day 7)
7. *The golem rises. Again.* — **fragment/ellipsis** (Day 8)
8. *For centuries we told this story. Then, one day, the golem opens its eyes — and doesn't stop.* — **historic present** (Day 9)

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Device Scope | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| Day 1–9 (C2) | One primary rhetorical device per session | Builds individual mastery of a single craft tool at a time |
| Day 10 (Bridge) | Mixed combo — all devices available at once | Tests the FINAL C2 skill: knowing which device to reach for in a given moment, not just knowing each one exists |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Literary essays on technology, speculative fiction, op-eds on AI ethics, philosophical commentary written for a general but sophisticated audience — any context where the writer must move seamlessly between multiple registers and devices within a single piece.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a short reflective piece on AI in literature or the human imagination — the golem, the uncanny valley, the ghost in the machine, or any angle that interests you. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and deliberately combine at least THREE different rhetorical devices from Days 1-9 (e.g., a litotes, a register-shift, and a historic-present moment).

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one sentence per word, each using a different device from the C2 toolkit so far.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Do you think AI, at some point, will blur the line between tool and something closer to a mind of its own?
2. Is there a piece of fiction — book, film, myth — that you think captures the uncanny valley particularly well?
3. Tell me about a moment in this topic where you genuinely felt we might be playing with fire.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 9 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: berapa banyak device dari Day 1-9 yang benar-benar berhasil dikombinasikan secara natural dalam tulisan user (sebutkan device mana yang teridentifikasi) + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal dua device baru yang belum dipakai user, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *by virtue of, insofar as* / native: *mind you, if anything*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing AI and imagination (e.g. **a mirror held up to humanity**, **take on a life of its own**, **uncharted territory**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it deepens the reflection — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any UNINTENTIONAL register slippage versus deliberate, controlled register-shifting. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| The AI start writing poem, is very strange to see. | The AI begins writing poetry — eerily, not merely strangely. | Shifting to present tense ("begins") plus the precise connotation of "eerily" over "strange" lands both the historic-present and connotation-precision devices at once. |
| This technology can be good or bad, we don't know yet. | Whether this technology proves a gift or a curse remains, for now, uncharted territory. | "Uncharted territory" plus the more balanced phrasing carries the same idea with Mastery-level craft instead of a flat hedge. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas. Ini sesi review gabungan — boleh secara eksplisit menyebut device mana dari Day 1-9 yang berhasil dipakai user, layaknya memberi "nilai rapor" singkat di akhir level.
- Error umum di topik ini: hanya memakai satu device saja (biasanya hyperbole atau idiom) padahal tujuan Day ini adalah kombinasi; device yang dipaksakan masuk tanpa benar-benar pas dengan konteks kalimat; kehilangan koherensi karena terlalu banyak device ditumpuk dalam satu kalimat yang sama.
- Template pujian: spesifik dan menyebut device by name — contoh: "That combo right there — the litotes in the opening, then the historic-present shift at the end — is exactly the kind of range this level was built toward."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user membuat catatan pribadi berisi satu device per Day yang sudah dikuasai, dan secara sadar mencoba menyelipkan minimal dua di antaranya setiap kali menulis sesuatu yang penting setelah ini.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you say that same point again, but this time with a deliberate understatement instead of a direct claim?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas — boleh menyinggung perjalanan dari Day 1 sampai Day 10 secara singkat.

---

#### 6. 🔗 PROMPT — Day 10 (Copy-Paste ke ChatGPT)


### DAY 11 — The Psychology of Persuasion in Advertising & Propaganda

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| a subliminal message | a message designed to influence someone below the level of conscious awareness |
| a scare tactic | a strategy that deliberately uses fear to influence someone's decision or behavior |
| pull at someone's heartstrings | to deliberately evoke strong emotion, especially sympathy, in order to persuade |
| buy into (an idea) | to come to believe in or accept an idea, often after being persuaded |
| smoke and mirrors | deception or a misleading explanation designed to obscure the truth |
| gaslight /ˈɡæs.laɪt/ | to manipulate someone into doubting their own perception or memory of reality |
| a loaded question | a question phrased so that any answer seems to confirm an assumption built into it |
| spin (something) | to present information in a way that creates a misleadingly favorable impression |
| a hidden agenda | an undisclosed motive behind someone's actions or proposals |
| a wolf in sheep's clothing | someone or something that appears harmless or trustworthy but is actually dangerous or deceptive |
| pull the wool over someone's eyes | to deceive someone, especially by hiding the truth from them |
| a dog whistle | a coded message that appeals to a particular group while appearing innocuous to others |
| a captive audience | a group of people who have no real choice but to watch or listen |
| peddle (an idea) | to promote or spread an idea persistently, often one that is dubious |
| a Trojan horse | something that appears beneficial or harmless but conceals a hidden, harmful intent |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Rhetorical Questions & Antithesis**

Advertising and propaganda rarely state their conclusion outright — they engineer the audience into reaching it themselves. Two devices do most of this work: the rhetorical question, which poses a question whose "obvious" answer does the persuading, and antithesis, which sharpens a claim by setting it against its opposite in parallel structure.

Three patterns:

1. **Rhetorical question for implied argument** — posing a question so the audience supplies the persuasive answer themselves.
   - *Why pay more for less?*
2. **Antithesis for persuasive contrast** — placing two opposing ideas in parallel structure to make a claim memorable and binary.
   - *It's not a luxury. It's a necessity.*
3. **Combined rhetorical question + antithesis** — stacking both devices for maximum persuasive force.
   - *Why choose ordinary, when extraordinary costs the same?*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Persuasive Structure | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Extended cleft sentences (it-cleft/what-cleft) for emphasis in formal argument | Isolates a single point for ANALYTICAL emphasis in formal, written persuasion |
| C2 | Rhetorical questions & antithesis (Why settle for less? / Not a luxury — a necessity.) | Exploits the audience's OWN reasoning and binary framing to bypass critical thinking — the psychological mechanism behind advertising and propaganda itself |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Advertising copy, political slogans, propaganda posters, persuasive speeches, marketing campaigns, op-eds designed to move public opinion — any context where the goal is to make the audience feel they reached a conclusion on their own.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a short piece of advertising copy or propaganda analysis — either crafting a persuasive pitch yourself, or analyzing how a real or invented campaign manipulates its audience. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate rhetorical question paired with antithesis.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one persuasive or analytical sentence per word.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Can you think of an advert or campaign that really pulled at your heartstrings? What made it work?
2. Where do you draw the line between clever persuasion and a scare tactic that's gone too far?
3. Write me a one-line slogan using a rhetorical question and antithesis together — sell me something, anything.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 10 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah rhetorical question/antithesis yang dipakai user benar-benar mengarahkan pembaca ke sebuah konklusi, atau hanya terasa seperti pertanyaan biasa + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu rhetorical question/antithesis baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *by the same token, insofar as* / native: *if anything, mind you*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing persuasion and propaganda (e.g. **a hidden agenda**, **smoke and mirrors**, **a wolf in sheep's clothing**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the analysis — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| This ad use fear to make people buy the product fast. | This ad leans on a scare tactic to rush people into buying. | "Scare tactic" is the precise term; "use fear" is a flat paraphrase that undersells the analysis. |
| Why you would choose less when you can have more for same price? | Why choose less, when more costs exactly the same? | Word order and ellipsis here are what make the rhetorical question land — the original buries the antithesis in clunky syntax. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas. Tidak menjelaskan ulang apa itu rhetorical question secara dasar — anggap user sudah paham konsep ini dari level sebelumnya.
- Error umum di topik ini: rhetorical question yang dijawab sendiri secara eksplisit (menghilangkan efek persuasifnya); antithesis yang dua sisinya tidak benar-benar paralel secara struktur; analisis propaganda yang hanya mendeskripsikan, bukan membongkar mekanisme psikologisnya.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft persuasi — contoh: "That antithesis — 'not a luxury, a necessity' — is exactly the binary framing real ad copy relies on."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user membongkar SATU iklan nyata setiap minggu dan mengidentifikasi device spesifik apa (rhetorical question, antithesis, scare tactic, dog whistle) yang dipakai — analisis konkret melatih kepekaan lebih cepat daripada teori.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Now turn that same slogan into a scare tactic instead — how does the persuasion shift?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

---

### DAY 12 — Code-Switching & the Multilingual Identity

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| code-switching | the practice of alternating between two or more languages, dialects, or registers within a conversation |
| a mother tongue | the first language a person learns and typically feels most natural in |
| a dominant language | the language a multilingual person uses most often or feels strongest in |
| linguistic identity | the sense of self shaped by the language(s) a person speaks and how they speak them |
| go native | to fully adopt the language, customs, or habits of another culture |
| straddle two worlds | to exist between, or belong partly to, two different cultures or identities at once |
| lost for words | momentarily unable to find the right words to express oneself |
| slip into (a dialect/accent) | to begin speaking in a particular dialect or accent without deciding to |
| colloquialism /kəˈloʊ.kwi.ə.lɪ.zəm/ | an informal word or phrase typical of everyday conversation |
| vernacular /vəˈnæk.jʊ.lər/ | the everyday, informal language spoken by ordinary people in a particular region or group |
| a third culture kid | a person raised in a culture different from their parents' or their own nationality |
| find one's voice | to develop the confidence and ability to express oneself authentically |
| a loanword | a word borrowed from one language and used in another, often without translation |
| native-like fluency | a level of language ability that closely resembles that of a native speaker |
| a linguistic chameleon | someone who shifts effortlessly between languages, dialects, or registers depending on context |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Register-Shifting Fluency (formal↔colloquial↔slang)**

This is not the same as switching registers for *context* (a sincere, situational shift) or for satirical *mismatch* (a deliberate joke). Here, register-shifting fluency is an expression of **identity** — multilingual and bicultural speakers often move between formal English, colloquial English, and slang within a single conversation, or even a single sentence, as a way of signaling which community they belong to in that moment.

Three patterns:

1. **Register-shifting for solidarity or distance** — choosing a more colloquial register to signal belonging, or a formal one to create distance.
   - *I was all formal in the meeting, obviously — but the second we got in the lift, it was straight back to "mate, that was painful."*
2. **Code-meshing** — blending formal vocabulary with colloquial or slang structure within the same utterance, rather than switching cleanly between them.
   - *He's incredibly articulate, yeah, but he'll still drop an "innit" at the end of a sentence — and somehow it works.*
3. **Strategic register slippage as performance** — deliberately breaking an expected formal register to signal authenticity or rapport.
   - *I could give you the polished answer. Or I could just tell you straight: it was a mess.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Register Shift | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Conscious formal↔natural register switching within a session | A sincere shift appropriate to a genuinely CHANGING CONTEXT |
| C2 (Day 12) | Register-shifting fluency across formal↔colloquial↔slang, often within the same exchange | A marker of MULTILINGUAL/MULTI-COMMUNITY IDENTITY — signaling belonging or authenticity, not just context-appropriateness |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Multilingual households, diaspora communities, code-switching in the workplace, memoir writing about bicultural upbringing, comedy about immigrant or multilingual identity — any context where moving between registers IS the point being made, not just a stylistic choice.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write about an experience of code-switching or living between languages/cultures — your own, or someone else's. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate moment of register-shifting or code-meshing within a sentence.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one sentence per word reflecting on language, identity, or belonging.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Do you ever catch yourself slipping into a different accent or dialect depending on who you're talking to?
2. Is there a word in your mother tongue that you think defies translation — one you'd consider a loanword if it ever crossed into English?
3. Would you describe yourself as a linguistic chameleon? Give me an example of when you've switched registers without even noticing.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 11 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah register-shift yang dipakai user benar-benar terasa sebagai identity marker yang disengaja, atau hanya inkonsistensi nada yang tidak disengaja + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu momen code-meshing baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *insofar as, by virtue of* / native: *mind you, fair enough*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing multilingual identity (e.g. **straddle two worlds**, **find one's voice**, **a third culture kid**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it deepens the reflection — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any UNINTENTIONAL register slippage versus deliberate, identity-driven register-shifting. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| When I talk with my family I use different language style than with my colleague. | When I'm with family, I slip into a completely different register than I do with colleagues. | "Slip into a register" is the precise native phrasing; "different language style" reads as a flat translation. |
| I sometimes forget word in English because my mother tongue is stronger. | I sometimes find myself lost for words in English, simply because my mother tongue runs deeper. | "Lost for words" is the natural collocation; "forget word" is a literal calque from the original idea. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas. Tidak menjelaskan ulang apa itu code-switching secara dasar — anggap user sudah familiar dengan konsep ini, terutama karena ini relevan dengan pengalaman pribadi banyak user.
- Error umum di topik ini: register-shift yang disebutkan tapi tidak benar-benar ditunjukkan dalam tulisan; mendeskripsikan multilingualism secara terlalu generik tanpa detail konkret; kehilangan kesempatan menunjukkan code-meshing yang sebenarnya umum terjadi secara natural.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft identitas — contoh: "That shift from formal to 'mate, that was painful' captures exactly how natural code-switching feels — not performed, just lived."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user memperhatikan momen nyata di kehidupan mereka sendiri di mana mereka berpindah register tanpa sadar, dan menuliskannya secara spesifik — detail personal jauh lebih kuat daripada generalisasi tentang multilingualism.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you say that same sentence twice — once in your most formal register, once in your most casual?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

---

#### 6. 🔗 PROMPT — Day 12 (Copy-Paste ke ChatGPT)

```
Topik: Code-Switching & the Multilingual Identity

Gunakan Full English untuk SEMUA penjelasan, instruksi, koreksi, dan feedback — TANPA terjemahan atau catatan Bahasa Indonesia dalam bentuk apapun, termasuk di tabel Box of Words (tidak ada kolom Bahasa Indonesia sama sekali).
Koreksi dibuat SINGKAT dan TAJAM — satu kalimat per error, gaya native menegur native.
Tampilkan phonetic symbol UK setelah setiap kosakata dalam tanda / /.

LANGKAH 1 — Sapa santai dalam English, sebutkan ini Day 12 dan singgung sekilas topik Day 11 (The Psychology of Persuasion in Advertising & Propaganda) sebagai vocab refresh sebelum lanjut ke topik baru. Lalu langsung tampilkan:
📦 Box of Words — Use EXACTLY these 15 words (do not add or substitute any):
code-switching, a mother tongue, a dominant language, linguistic identity, go native, straddle two worlds, lost for words, slip into (a dialect/accent), colloquialism, vernacular, a third culture kid, find one's voice, a loanword, native-like fluency, a linguistic chameleon
Display in a 2-column table only: Kosakata+phonetic | English Definition. Add UK phonetics where not shown.
✍️ Writing Challenge — Mode Cerita (8-10 kalimat tentang pengalaman code-switching atau hidup di antara bahasa/budaya, pakai 5 kata BOW + minimal 1 momen register-shifting/code-meshing dalam satu kalimat) dan Mode Kilat (5 kalimat, 1 per kata BOW, reflektif tentang bahasa/identitas).
Grammar fokus hari ini: Register-Shifting Fluency (formal↔colloquial↔slang) — jelaskan singkat kenapa ini beda dari register switching C1 (sincere shift sesuai konteks): di C2, register-shifting yang fluent across formal-colloquial-slang adalah PENANDA IDENTITAS multilingual/multi-komunitas, bukan sekadar penyesuaian konteks.

LANGKAH 2 — Setelah aku kirim tulisan, kalau ada SATU pola error paling signifikan (terutama soal register-shift yang disebutkan tapi tidak benar-benar ditunjukkan, atau inkonsistensi nada yang tidak disengaja), tandai dulu HANYA lokasi + jenis errornya dalam satu kalimat tajam tanpa kasih jawaban (Self-Check Pertama), tunggu responsku. Kalau tulisanku sudah ≥95% benar, lewati langsung. Lalu jalankan Koreksi 8 Langkah: (1) Koreksi Writing (tabel Kalimat Asli | Kalimat Benar | Why singkat, tanpa kolom Bahasa Indonesia), (2) Analisa BOW + sertakan 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 11 (vocab refresh), (3) Analisa CEFR (saran mempertahankan Mastery), (4) 5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph, (5) Discourse Markers, (6) Craft & Lexical Chunks — 2-3 lexical chunks native speakers use discussing multilingual identity (e.g. **straddle two worlds**, **find one's voice**, **a third culture kid**); check if used naturally (✅); suggest one, (7) Register/Formality Check — Spot any UNINTENTIONAL register slippage versus deliberate, identity-driven register-shifting. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent, (8) Speaking Challenge (3 pertanyaan tentang accents, mother tongues, dan linguistic chameleons). If my writing is blank or not in English, ask me to write first.

LANGKAH 3 — Kalau aku aktifkan mode suara dan ketik "Let's start speaking!", ajukan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, koreksi singkat dan langsung.
```

### DAY 13 — The Art of the Toast: Celebration, Ritual & Spoken Tradition

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| a toast | a short speech in which people raise their glasses to honor someone or something |
| raise a glass (to) | to lift one's drink in a gesture of honor or celebration toward someone |
| propose a toast | to formally suggest that everyone raise their glasses in honor of someone |
| here's to | a phrase used to introduce the subject of a toast |
| a red-letter day | a notably happy, memorable, or important day worth celebrating |
| heartfelt /ˈhɑːt.felt/ | deeply and genuinely sincere |
| bask in (the moment) | to enjoy and savor a pleasurable situation or atmosphere fully |
| an occasion to remember | an event significant or memorable enough to be looked back on fondly |
| festivities /fesˈtɪv.ɪ.tiz/ | activities and events organized as part of a celebration |
| a parting word | a final remark, especially one offered at the close of a speech or gathering |
| in high spirits | feeling cheerful, lively, and full of enthusiasm |
| a joyous occasion | an event marked by happiness and celebration |
| mark the occasion | to do something special to recognize or celebrate an event |
| raise the roof | to celebrate so enthusiastically that the noise seems to lift the ceiling |
| merriment /ˈmer.i.mənt/ | cheerful enjoyment, laughter, and fun, especially at a celebration |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Apposition & Embedded Asides**

A scripted-sounding toast undercuts its own sincerity. Native speakers keep a toast feeling live and spoken — even when carefully prepared — through two structures: apposition, which renames a person with a warm or honorific phrase right after naming them, and embedded asides, brief parenthetical remarks dropped mid-sentence that sound spontaneous rather than rehearsed.

Three patterns:

1. **Apposition for warm identification** — renaming someone with an affectionate or honorific phrase immediately after naming them.
   - *To Sarah — my oldest friend, partner in every disaster — happy birthday.*
2. **Embedded aside for spontaneous warmth** — inserting a brief, conversational remark mid-sentence to feel live and personal, not scripted.
   - *Here's to the happy couple — and yes, Dave, you can finally stop asking when this would happen — may your life together be everything you've dreamed of.*
3. **Embedded aside for self-deprecating humor** — a quick parenthetical joke about the speaker themselves, common in toasts to ease nerves and warm the room.
   - *I wrote this speech three times — don't worry, this is the short version — so let's get to it.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Structure | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Multi-clause embedding (subordinating ideas into one dense, complex sentence) | Compresses information for ANALYTICAL density in writing |
| C2 (Day 13) | Apposition & embedded asides (commas/dashes inserting warm or spontaneous remarks mid-sentence) | Creates SPOKEN, LIVE warmth — the hallmark of toasts and ritual speech, where sounding scripted would undercut sincerity |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Wedding toasts, birthday speeches, retirement send-offs, holiday gatherings, award acceptance speeches — any ritual occasion where the spoken word needs to feel personal and present, not read from a page.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a short toast for someone — a friend, family member, colleague, or even a fictional character — marking a happy occasion. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate apposition and one embedded aside.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one celebratory, toast-style sentence per word.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. If you had to propose a toast right now, with no preparation, who would it be for and what would you say?
2. What's the most memorable toast or speech you've ever heard at a celebration — what made it land?
3. Give me a toast that includes at least one embedded aside — a little joke or remark slipped in mid-sentence.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 12 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah apposition/embedded aside yang dipakai user benar-benar terasa spontan dan hangat, atau malah terbaca kaku seperti teks yang dibaca + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu apposition/embedded aside baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *by the same token, notwithstanding* / native: *mind you, fair enough*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use in toasts and celebratory speech (e.g. **raise a glass to**, **mark the occasion**, **an occasion to remember**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it elevates the ceremonial tone — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| To my friend who always support me, I want to say thank you. | To Maya — the friend who's never once let me down — thank you. | Naming her directly and using apposition makes the toast feel personal rather than generic. |
| Today is very happy day for all of us here. | Today is a red-letter day for all of us here. | "A red-letter day" is the precise, ceremonial collocation; "very happy day" undershoots the register this Day targets. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, tapi tetap hangat — toast adalah genre yang personal, jadi feedback boleh sedikit lebih warm tanpa kehilangan ketajaman.
- Error umum di topik ini: toast yang terlalu generik tanpa detail personal spesifik; apposition yang terasa ditempelkan, bukan mengalir natural; kehilangan momentum karena tidak ada embedded aside sama sekali, sehingga terasa seperti dibaca dari teks.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft toast — contoh: "That aside about Dave finally getting his answer — that's exactly the kind of live, spontaneous touch that makes a toast memorable."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user menyelipkan SATU detail personal yang sangat spesifik (bukan generik) di setiap toast yang mereka tulis — detail spesifik itulah yang membuat toast terasa tulus, bukan template.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you add one more embedded aside to that toast — something that would get a genuine laugh?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

---
