### DAY 14 — Dialects, Sociolects & the Politics of "Correct" English

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| a dialect /ˈdaɪ.ə.lekt/ | a regional or social variety of a language with distinct vocabulary, grammar, or pronunciation |
| a sociolect /ˈsoʊ.si.oʊ.lekt/ | a variety of language associated with a particular social group or class |
| prestige (linguistic) /presˈtiːʒ/ | the social status or value attached to a particular language variety |
| stigmatize /ˈstɪɡ.mə.taɪz/ | to regard or treat a way of speaking (or a person) as shameful or inferior |
| Standard English | the variety of English regarded as the formal, "correct" norm, typically taught in schools |
| talk down to (someone) | to speak to someone as though they are less intelligent or important |
| put on airs | to behave or speak as though one is superior, often by affecting a "proper" accent |
| linguistic gatekeeping | the act of excluding or judging people based on how they speak |
| a shibboleth /ˈʃɪb.ə.lɛθ/ | a word or way of speaking that distinguishes members of one group from outsiders |
| talk the talk | to convincingly use the language and style associated with a particular group |
| accent bias | prejudice or discrimination against someone based on the way they pronounce words |
| broken English | a term, often controversial, for non-standard or non-fluent spoken English |
| the King's English | a term for formally correct, traditionally prestigious British English |
| a pidgin /ˈpɪdʒ.ɪn/ | a simplified language that develops between groups without a shared native language |
| a creole /ˈkriː.oʊl/ | a stable, fully developed language that originates from a pidgin becoming a community's native tongue |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Comparative Register Awareness**

At C2, the question shifts from "which register should I use?" (a practical choice) to "why is one register treated as more correct than another?" (a critical one). Comparative structures become a tool for naming and questioning assumed linguistic hierarchies — recognizing that "Standard English" is not inherently superior, only socially dominant.

Three patterns:

1. **Comparative used to flatten an assumed hierarchy** — explicitly denying a hierarchy that is often taken for granted.
   - *Standard English isn't more grammatical than a regional dialect — it's simply the dialect that gained institutional power.*
2. **Concessive comparison** — acknowledging a real difference while reframing its significance.
   - *Yes, it's less "formal" by certain standards — but it's no less expressive for it.*
3. **Meta-commentary on register itself** — naming and commenting on a register choice while making it, a self-aware move.
   - *I could "talk proper," as they say — but this is how my grandmother actually spoke.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Register Approach | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Consistently formal, academically cautious register (hedged, distanced, impersonal) | Treats formal register as the DEFAULT for credibility and objectivity |
| C2 (Day 14) | Comparative register awareness — analyzing, and sometimes deliberately choosing, a "non-standard" register | Treats register itself as a POLITICAL and social choice — "correctness" is a matter of power, not linguistic superiority |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Sociolinguistics discussions, debates about accent discrimination in hiring or media, literature written in dialect or creole, classroom conversations about "proper" English, op-eds on linguistic prejudice — any context where the legitimacy of a way of speaking is itself the subject.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a reflective piece about dialects, accents, or the idea of "correct" English — your own experience, or an observation about how language and social judgment intersect. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate comparative structure that questions an assumed hierarchy.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one sentence per word reflecting on dialect, prestige, or linguistic identity.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Have you ever felt judged — or judged someone else — based on their accent or dialect?
2. Do you think "Standard English" deserves the prestige it has, or is that prestige just historical accident?
3. Give me an example of a shibboleth — a word or phrase that immediately marks someone as an insider or outsider in a group you know well.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 13 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah comparative structure yang dipakai user benar-benar membongkar sebuah asumsi hierarki, atau hanya membandingkan secara netral tanpa sudut pandang kritis + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu comparative/concessive structure baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *by virtue of, notwithstanding* / native: *mind you, if anything*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing dialects and language politics (e.g. **linguistic gatekeeping**, **put on airs**, **talk the talk**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the critical angle — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| Standard English is more correct than other dialect. | Standard English isn't more correct than other dialects — it's simply more prestigious. | The original repeats the very assumption this Day asks you to question; the corrected version names the comparison critically instead. |
| People sometimes judge my accent and think I talk broken English. | People sometimes hear my accent and dismiss it as broken English — unfairly. | "Dismiss it as" plus the qualifying "unfairly" shows critical awareness of the term's bias, rather than simply repeating it. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, tapi tetap peka terhadap sensitivitas topik ini (bias bahasa bisa personal bagi banyak user) — pujian dan koreksi tetap tulus tanpa terasa menghakimi.
- Error umum di topik ini: membandingkan dialek/aksen secara netral tanpa benar-benar membongkar asumsi hierarki yang mendasarinya; memakai istilah seperti "broken English" tanpa kesadaran kritis terhadap konotasinya; generalisasi tentang "bahasa yang benar" tanpa menyebut siapa yang menentukan standar itu.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft kritis — contoh: "That comparative structure — 'not more correct, just more prestigious' — is exactly the kind of reframing this topic is built around."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mengidentifikasi SATU asumsi tentang 'bahasa yang benar' yang mereka sendiri pegang tanpa sadar, dan menuliskan argumen balik terhadap asumsi itu — refleksi personal jauh lebih kuat daripada teori abstrak.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you rephrase that same point as a comparative that openly challenges the hierarchy, instead of just describing it?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

### DAY 15 — The Philosophy of Silence: What We Choose Not to Say

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| silence speaks volumes | a saying meaning that someone's silence communicates a great deal without words |
| an awkward silence | an uncomfortable pause in conversation, often signaling tension or unease |
| a pregnant pause | a brief silence heavy with unspoken meaning or anticipation |
| left unsaid | not expressed in words, even though understood or implied |
| trail off /treɪl ɒf/ | to gradually stop speaking, often as a sentence fades into silence |
| bite one's tongue | to deliberately stop oneself from saying something, often out of restraint |
| read the silence | to correctly interpret the unspoken meaning behind someone's lack of words |
| a loaded silence | a silence that carries strong, often tense, unspoken emotion or implication |
| stay tight-lipped | to deliberately refuse to share information or speak about something |
| the elephant in the room | an obvious problem or issue that everyone notices but avoids discussing |
| leave something unspoken | to deliberately choose not to say something, even though it is understood |
| a deafening silence | a silence so charged or absolute that it feels overwhelming |
| reticence /ˈret.ɪ.səns/ | a tendency to be reserved or reluctant to speak about one's thoughts |
| what goes unsaid | the meaning or message conveyed by what is deliberately not spoken |
| (it) goes without saying | used to indicate that something is so obvious it requires no explicit statement |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Advanced Ellipsis for Rhetorical/Emotional Effect**

By C2, ellipsis is no longer just a tool for casual economy — it becomes a deliberate rhetorical weapon. Withholding words, breaking off mid-sentence, or simply staying silent can carry more meaning than finishing the thought ever could.

Three patterns:

1. **Aposiopesis** — breaking off mid-sentence, usually from overwhelming emotion, leaving the rest implied.
   - *I wanted to tell her everything, but when she looked at me like that, I just... I couldn't.*
2. **Strategic omission** — deliberately withholding the obvious conclusion, trusting the listener to reach it alone.
   - *I won't say what he did. I'll just say the trial isn't over yet.*
3. **Meaningful silence as a complete response** — letting silence itself stand as a full, deliberate answer.
   - *She asked if he regretted it. He said nothing. That was the answer.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Ellipsis Type | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C2 (Day 8) | Conversational ellipsis (dropping subjects/auxiliaries in casual banter — *Seen him? / Coming?*) | Reflects native ECONOMY and RHYTHM in fast, casual speech |
| C2 (Day 15) | Advanced ellipsis/aposiopesis (breaking off, withholding, silence-as-answer) | Carries deliberate EMOTIONAL or RHETORICAL weight — the silence itself becomes the message |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Literary fiction and memoir, courtroom drama, emotionally charged dialogue, political non-answers, therapy or conflict conversations, poetry — any context where what's NOT said matters as much as what is.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a reflective or narrative piece about a moment where silence said more than words could — your own experience, or an imagined scene. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate aposiopesis or moment of strategic omission.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one sentence per word reflecting on silence, restraint, or the unspoken.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Tell me about a time an awkward silence or a pregnant pause said more than any words could have.
2. Is there something you've deliberately left unsaid to someone — and do you think that was the right call?
3. Give me a sentence that trails off mid-thought, the way we do when emotion takes over — let it just... stop.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 14 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah aposiopesis/strategic omission yang dipakai user benar-benar terasa sebagai silence yang bermakna, atau hanya kalimat yang terpotong tanpa efek emosional + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu momen aposiopesis/silence-as-answer baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *notwithstanding, by the same token* / native: *mind you, then again*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing silence and restraint (e.g. **the elephant in the room**, **a loaded silence**, **stay tight-lipped**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it deepens the emotional weight — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| Nobody talk about the problem even though everyone know it exist. | Nobody mentioned the elephant in the room, even though everyone knew it was there. | The idiom carries exactly the implication the original sentence states outright — naming it directly undercuts the point. |
| I want to say sorry but I stopped because I too emotional. | I wanted to say I was sorry, but I just... I couldn't get the words out. | The trailing aposiopesis enacts the very emotion the original only describes. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, tapi peka — topik silence sering personal dan emosional, jadi feedback tetap tulus tanpa terasa mengintervensi area sensitif user.
- Error umum di topik ini: mendeskripsikan keheningan/emosi secara eksplisit alih-alih membiarkan struktur kalimat (trailing off, omission) yang melakukan pekerjaan itu; aposiopesis yang terasa dipaksakan karena tidak didahului build-up emosional yang cukup; menyebutkan "the elephant in the room" tapi langsung menjelaskannya, menghilangkan efek silence-nya sendiri.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft silence — contoh: "That trailing line — 'I just... I couldn't' — does more emotional work than a full explanation ever would."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mengidentifikasi SATU momen nyata di hidup mereka di mana diam justru menyampaikan lebih banyak daripada kata-kata, lalu menuliskannya dengan membiarkan keheningan itu "berbicara" lewat struktur kalimat, bukan deskripsi langsung.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you tell me that same moment again, but this time let your voice trail off exactly where the silence mattered most?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

### DAY 16 — Comedy Writing & the Architecture of a Joke

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| a setup | the opening part of a joke that establishes context before the punchline lands |
| the rule of three | a comedic principle in which two items establish a pattern that a third subverts |
| misdirection | leading an audience's expectations one way before subverting them for comic effect |
| a slow burn | a joke or reaction that builds gradually rather than landing immediately |
| land (a joke) | to successfully deliver a joke so that it gets the intended reaction |
| bomb (on stage) | to fail completely to get any laughs during a comedic performance |
| a callback | a joke that references an earlier moment in the same set, rewarding an attentive audience |
| punch up | to direct comedy at those with more power or status than the comedian |
| punch down | to direct comedy at those with less power or status, often considered poor form |
| a heckler | an audience member who interrupts a performer with mocking or critical remarks |
| corpsing /ˈkɔː.pɪŋ/ | breaking character by laughing uncontrollably during a performance |
| a comic beat | a deliberate pause in delivery used to control the rhythm of a joke |
| a one-liner | a short, self-contained joke delivered in a single sentence |
| bathos /ˈbeɪ.θɒs/ | an abrupt shift from the elevated to the trivial, often used for comic effect |
| a shaggy dog story | a long, rambling joke whose anticlimactic ending is itself the punchline |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Timing-Driven Sentence Structure (fragments for punchlines)**

By C2, comic timing isn't just performance — it's built into the grammar of the sentence itself. Deliberate fragments, delayed reveals, and broken rhythm can do the comedic work that a grammatically "complete" sentence would flatten.

Three patterns:

1. **Fragment as punchline** — ending a joke with a deliberate sentence fragment for comic punch.
   - *We had a plan. A really, really bad plan.*
2. **Delayed-reveal restructuring** — restructuring a sentence so the surprising element lands at the very end.
   - *What I did not expect, after all that planning, was for the cake to end up on the dog.*
3. **Tricolon-into-fragment (rule-of-three syntax)** — three parallel items building rhythm, then a fragment breaks the pattern for the punch.
   - *He brought wine. He brought flowers. He brought his ex-wife.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Device | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C2 (Day 2) | Lexical wordplay (puns, double entendre — humor built at the WORD level) | Comic effect through ambiguity or double meaning in vocabulary choice |
| C2 (Day 16) | Timing-driven sentence structure (fragments, delayed reveals, tricolon-into-fragment) | Comic effect through the RHYTHM and STRUCTURE of the sentence itself — timing as a grammatical choice |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Stand-up comedy writing, sitcom scripts, comedic essays, humorous storytelling, roast speeches — any context where the shape of the sentence is doing as much comedic work as the content.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a short comedic story or stand-up-style bit about something ordinary that went wrong. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate sentence fragment used as a punchline.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one comedic sentence per word.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Tell me about a joke that completely bombed when you told it — what went wrong with the timing?
2. Where's the line for you between a joke that punches up and one that punches down?
3. Give me a one-liner right now, off the top of your head — make it land.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 15 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah fragment/delayed-reveal yang dipakai user benar-benar menciptakan comic timing, atau hanya kalimat terpotong tanpa efek + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu fragment/delayed-reveal baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *notwithstanding, by the same token* / native: *mind you, if anything*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing comedy craft (e.g. **a slow burn**, **punch up**, **a comic beat**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the comic precision — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| I told a joke but nobody laughed and it was very embarrassing for me. | I told the joke. Silence. Pure, unfiltered silence. | Breaking into fragments enacts the awkward beat the original sentence only describes. |
| That comedian make jokes about poor people and it not funny, it just mean. | That comedian punches down at people with less power — and it lands as cruelty, not comedy. | "Punches down" names the exact ethical failure; "make jokes about poor people" is a flat paraphrase. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, dan boleh sedikit playful — topik ini secara alami mengundang humor dalam feedback itu sendiri, tanpa kehilangan ketajaman koreksi.
- Error umum di topik ini: punchline yang dijelaskan alih-alih ditunjukkan lewat struktur kalimat; fragment yang dipaksakan tanpa build-up yang cukup sehingga tidak terasa seperti timing, hanya kalimat putus; gagal membedakan punch up dari punch down dalam analisis humor.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft timing — contoh: "That fragment — 'A really, really bad plan.' — is exactly the kind of beat that makes a setup pay off."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user menulis ulang satu lelucon favorit mereka dengan sengaja memecah kalimat penutupnya menjadi fragment, lalu membandingkan versi mana yang lebih landed — latihan craft langsung lebih efektif daripada teori timing.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Now tell me that same joke again, but this time, really hold the pause before the punchline."
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

### DAY 17 — Legal Rhetoric & the Art of the Closing Argument

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| a closing argument | the final persuasive speech a lawyer delivers summarizing the case before a verdict |
| take the stand | to testify as a witness in court |
| cross-examine | to question a witness from the opposing side, especially to test their testimony |
| hammer home (a point) | to emphasize a point forcefully and repeatedly for persuasive effect |
| circumstantial evidence | indirect evidence that suggests a conclusion without proving it directly |
| an alibi /ˈæl.ɪ.baɪ/ | evidence or a claim that someone was elsewhere when an alleged crime occurred |
| paint a picture (for the jury) | to vividly describe events so an audience can clearly visualize them |
| an airtight case | a case built on evidence so strong it has no apparent weaknesses |
| the smoking gun | a definitive piece of evidence that proves guilt or wrongdoing beyond doubt |
| leave no stone unturned | to make every possible effort to investigate or search for something thoroughly |
| a star witness | the most compelling and persuasive witness in a case |
| plant a seed of doubt | to subtly introduce doubt into the minds of an audience or jury |
| seal someone's fate | to determine an outcome for someone that can no longer be avoided |
| rest one's case | to formally conclude presenting evidence and arguments, especially in court |
| the moment of truth | the critical point at which a decision or outcome is finally revealed |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Cumulative Sentences & Climactic Ordering**

A closing argument doesn't just state facts — it builds them, piece by piece, toward a final, undeniable point. Two structures drive this: the cumulative sentence, which starts with a core clause and layers on modifying detail, and climactic ordering, which arranges items so the most significant lands last.

Three patterns:

1. **Cumulative sentence build** — starting with a core clause, then layering modifying details that accumulate weight.
   - *She lied about the alibi — calmly, convincingly, and without a single moment of hesitation.*
2. **Climactic ordering (least to most significant)** — arranging a series of clauses or items from minor to most damning.
   - *He had the motive. He had the opportunity. He had blood on his shirt.*
3. **Cumulative + climactic combined for closing-argument crescendo** — building detail across several clauses, each escalating toward the final, most damning point.
   - *Members of the jury, consider the evidence: the timeline that doesn't add up, the alibi that falls apart under scrutiny, and finally — the fingerprint that was never supposed to be there.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Structure | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Hedged, qualification-driven argumentation (insofar as, burden of proof, it follows that) | Builds a case through cautious LOGICAL qualification in formal written argument |
| C2 (Day 17) | Cumulative sentences & climactic ordering (layered detail building to a final, damning point) | Builds a case through accumulating RHETORICAL MOMENTUM — persuasion through escalating concrete detail, not hedged logic |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Courtroom closing arguments, legal dramas, debate speeches, persuasive essays building toward a final claim, true-crime narration — any context where a series of details must escalate toward one undeniable conclusion.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a closing argument — real, fictional, or for a mock trial of your own invention. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate cumulative or climactically-ordered sentence.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one persuasive, courtroom-style sentence per word.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. If you had to build a closing argument for the most trivial case imaginable, what would it be about?
2. What's more persuasive to you — an airtight case built on hard evidence, or a star witness who's simply convincing to watch?
3. Give me three escalating pieces of "evidence" for something ridiculous, ending on the most damning one — go.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 16 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah cumulative sentence/climactic ordering yang dipakai user benar-benar membangun momentum ke titik klimaks, atau hanya daftar detail tanpa eskalasi + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu cumulative/climactic structure baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *by virtue of, in light of* / native: *mind you, when it comes down to it*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use in legal rhetoric (e.g. **hammer home a point**, **an airtight case**, **the smoking gun**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the persuasive force — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| The evidence show he is guilty, there is many proof against him. | Consider the evidence: the timeline that doesn't hold up, the alibi that collapses under scrutiny, and the fingerprint that was never supposed to be there. | The corrected version builds cumulative detail toward a climax; the original simply asserts the conclusion. |
| The witness said something but I am not sure if it true. | The witness took the stand — and what she said planted a seed of doubt no closing argument could undo. | Naming the specific courtroom action and idiom does the persuasive work the vague original cannot. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, dan tegas — gaya closing argument secara alami mengundang nada yang lebih assertive dibanding Day-Day sebelumnya, feedback boleh mencerminkan energi itu.
- Error umum di topik ini: menyatakan konklusi langsung tanpa membangun detail yang mengeskalasi terlebih dahulu; daftar bukti yang datar, tidak diurutkan dari kurang ke paling signifikan; kehilangan momentum karena climactic point diletakkan di awal, bukan di akhir.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft retoris — contoh: "That escalation — motive, opportunity, blood on his shirt — is textbook climactic ordering. The jury never saw it coming, and that's exactly the point."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mengambil satu argumen sehari-hari yang mereka buat secara datar, lalu menulis ulang dengan urutan climactic — detail kecil dulu, baru poin paling kuat di akhir — latihan ini melatih insting timing retoris jauh lebih cepat daripada teori.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Now reorder that same evidence — what happens if you save the weakest point for last instead?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

---

### DAY 18 — The Ethics of Persuasion: Where Does Manipulation Begin?

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| an ethical dilemma | a situation requiring a choice between two or more morally conflicting options |
| undue influence | improper pressure that overrides someone's free and informed decision-making |
| informed consent | agreement to something given with full understanding of the relevant facts and implications |
| a grey area | a situation that is not clearly right or wrong, open to interpretation |
| exploit (a weakness) | to take unfair advantage of a vulnerability for one's own benefit |
| a moral compass | an internal sense guiding a person's judgment of right and wrong |
| the lesser of two evils | the less harmful of two undesirable options, when neither is good |
| a power imbalance | a situation where one party holds significantly more influence or control than another |
| prey on (someone's fears) | to exploit someone's fears or vulnerabilities for personal gain |
| the ends justify the means | the belief that a good outcome makes any method used to achieve it acceptable |
| a clear conscience | a state of feeling free from guilt because one has acted rightly |
| by any means necessary | using whatever methods are required to achieve something, regardless of ethical concern |
| weigh on one's conscience | to cause someone persistent guilt or moral unease |
| a moral high ground | a position of greater ethical legitimacy than an opposing party |
| give someone the benefit of the doubt | to assume good intent in someone's actions despite uncertainty |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Modal Nuance for Moral Stance**

At C2, moral judgment is rarely stated as flat fact. Modal verbs let a writer take a position on right and wrong while precisely calibrating how certain, retrospective, or conditional that judgment is.

Three patterns:

1. **Retrospective moral modal (should have / ought to have)** — judging a past action against a moral standard.
   - *He ought to have known the campaign was manipulative — ignorance is no excuse at this level.*
2. **Hedged moral claim (might / could be argued)** — making a moral judgment while leaving room for nuance or counter-argument.
   - *One could argue it's manipulation; one could just as easily argue it's simply good marketing.*
3. **Obligation vs. permission contrast (must/should vs. can/may)** — distinguishing what's technically permissible from what's morally required.
   - *You may be allowed to do this legally — that doesn't mean you should.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Modal Use | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Modal + counterfactual fusion (had it been..., were it to...) for testing logical culpability in philosophical argument | Tests whether a factor was logically NECESSARY for moral responsibility |
| C2 (Day 18) | Modal nuance for moral stance (ought to have, might, must vs. may) in everyday persuasive argument | Calibrates the SPEAKER'S OWN certainty and moral commitment — making a judgment while hedging exactly how firmly it's held |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Op-eds on marketing ethics, debates about manipulation in politics or advertising, personal reflections on moral grey areas, ethics panels, conversations about where persuasion crosses into exploitation.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a reflective piece on a real or hypothetical case where persuasion arguably crossed into manipulation — an ad campaign, a negotiation, a relationship, a political message. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate modal used to calibrate a moral judgment.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one sentence per word reflecting on ethics, persuasion, or manipulation.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Where do you personally draw the line between persuasion and manipulation?
2. Can you think of a time someone gave you the benefit of the doubt when you maybe didn't deserve it — or vice versa?
3. Do you think the ends ever truly justify the means? Give me a real example, not a hypothetical.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 17 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah modal yang dipakai user benar-benar mengkalibrasi nuansa moral (kepastian, retrospektif, kondisional), atau hanya pernyataan flat tanpa nuansa + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu modal nuance baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *insofar as, by virtue of* / native: *then again, fair enough*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing ethics of persuasion (e.g. **a power imbalance**, **a moral high ground**, **the lesser of two evils**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the moral precision — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| The company is wrong because they manipulate people emotion to sell product. | The company ought to have known that exploiting people's fears to sell a product crosses an ethical line. | "Ought to have known" calibrates retrospective moral judgment; the original simply asserts wrongness without that nuance. |
| Maybe it manipulation, maybe not, nobody can be sure. | One could argue it's manipulation; one could just as easily argue it's simply persuasive marketing. | The hedged modal construction does precisely the nuanced moral work the vague original gestures at but never executes. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, dan reflektif — topik etika mengundang nuansa, jadi feedback boleh mengakui kompleksitas moral tanpa kehilangan ketajaman linguistik.
- Error umum di topik ini: pernyataan moral yang flat tanpa modal nuance sama sekali; mencampur "can/may" (izin) dengan "should/must" (obligasi moral) secara tidak sengaja; argumen etika yang tidak benar-benar mengkalibrasi tingkat kepastian penulis sendiri.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft nuansa moral — contoh: "That shift from 'may' to 'should' — 'you may be allowed to, that doesn't mean you should' — is exactly the kind of modal precision this topic rewards."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mengambil satu keputusan etis yang mereka buat baru-baru ini, lalu menuliskan ulang penjelasannya dengan sengaja mengkalibrasi modal (ought to have, could, must vs may) — refleksi pribadi melatih nuansa moral lebih cepat daripada teori abstrak.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you say that same judgment again, but hedge it this time — 'one could argue...' instead of stating it as fact?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

### DAY 19 — Poetry, Song Lyrics & the Economy of Language

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| a refrain | a recurring line or phrase repeated throughout a song or poem |
| a hook | a catchy, memorable musical or lyrical phrase designed to stick in the listener's mind |
| an earworm | a song or melody that gets stuck in one's mind and repeats involuntarily |
| cadence /ˈkeɪ.dəns/ | the rhythmic flow or rise and fall of language, especially in speech or verse |
| a couplet /ˈkʌp.lɪt/ | two consecutive lines of verse, typically rhyming and matched in length or meter |
| scansion /ˈskæn.ʃən/ | the analysis of a verse's rhythmic pattern and meter |
| distill (an idea) | to express the essential meaning of something in the fewest possible words |
| a kernel of truth | a small but significant element of truth within something larger or exaggerated |
| an extended metaphor | a metaphor developed and sustained across multiple lines or an entire piece |
| lyricism /ˈlɪr.ɪ.sɪ.zəm/ | the quality of expressing emotion or beauty through language, especially in writing or song |
| an internal rhyme | a rhyme occurring within a single line of verse, rather than at the line's end |
| a volta /ˈvɒl.tə/ | a turn or shift in argument or emotion within a poem, especially a sonnet |
| economy of language | the practice of conveying meaning with the fewest possible words |
| pack a punch | to have a strong, powerful, or memorable effect |
| less is more | the principle that simplicity or minimalism often communicates more effectively than excess |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Compression & Implication**

Poetry and song lyrics rarely explain — they compress. A handful of words, placed precisely, can imply an entire emotional truth that explanation would only dilute.

Three patterns:

1. **Compressed imagery standing in for explanation** — a single concrete image implying a larger emotional truth without stating it.
   - *Empty chair. Cold coffee. Six a.m.*
2. **Implication through juxtaposition** — placing two images or lines side by side so their relationship implies meaning the words never state directly.
   - *He kept the ring. She kept the keys.*
3. **Compression via omission of connective logic** — removing the explanatory link between cause and effect, trusting the audience to supply it.
   - *You left. The garden didn't.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Device | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C2 (Day 15) | Advanced ellipsis/aposiopesis (breaking off, withholding, silence-as-answer) | Carries deliberate EMOTIONAL/RHETORICAL weight — silence itself becomes the message in spoken narrative |
| C2 (Day 19) | Compression & implication (imagery, juxtaposition, omitted connective logic) | Maximizes meaning-per-word as an ARTISTIC/POETIC craft principle — implication replaces explanation in lyrics and verse |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Songwriting, poetry, greeting-card verse, advertising slogans built on lyrical compression, literary fiction with poetic prose passages — any context where fewer words must carry more weight.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a short poem or song lyric — about anything: love, loss, a memory, an ordinary moment. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate moment of compression or implication (an image or juxtaposition standing in for explanation).

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one compressed, image-driven sentence per word.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. What's a song lyric or line of poetry that's stuck with you — an earworm, in a sense — and why do you think it works?
2. Can you compress a memory of yours into just three words, the way a refrain might?
3. Give me an extended metaphor, right now, comparing your day to something completely unrelated.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 18 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah compression/implication yang dipakai user benar-benar membiarkan image melakukan pekerjaan emosional, atau malah menjelaskan terlalu banyak + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu momen compression/implication baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *by the same token, notwithstanding* / native: *then again, if anything*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing poetry and lyrics (e.g. **pack a punch**, **less is more**, **a kernel of truth**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the compression — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| I am very sad because she left me and the house feel empty now. | She left. The house didn't stop being full — it just stopped being hers. | The compressed, juxtaposed version implies the grief the original states outright, and lands with far more weight. |
| This song has a part that repeat many times and it easy to remember. | This song's refrain is the kind of hook that turns into an earworm by the second listen. | Naming the precise craft terms does the descriptive work that the vague paraphrase cannot. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, dan sedikit lebih liris — topik ini mengundang bahasa yang lebih evocative dalam feedback itu sendiri, tanpa kehilangan ketajaman koreksi.
- Error umum di topik ini: menjelaskan emosi secara eksplisit alih-alih membiarkan image/juxtaposition melakukan pekerjaan itu; metafora yang tidak benar-benar diperpanjang (extended) melewati satu baris; kehilangan economy of language karena terlalu banyak kata penjelas di sekitar image yang sudah kuat.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft compression — contoh: "'He kept the ring. She kept the keys.' — that juxtaposition says more about the breakup than a full paragraph could."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mengambil satu kalimat penjelas yang panjang dari tulisan mereka sendiri, lalu memampatkannya menjadi satu image atau juxtaposition singkat — latihan memampatkan ini melatih insting "less is more" jauh lebih cepat daripada teori puitis.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you compress that same image down to even fewer words — what's the absolute minimum that still lands?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

---

### DAY 20 — The Art of the Apology: Sincerity, Spin & Public Accountability

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| a non-apology | a statement that mimics the form of an apology while avoiding genuine responsibility |
| mistakes were made | a deliberately vague, agentless phrase used to acknowledge a problem without naming who caused it |
| take full responsibility | to openly accept blame and accountability for one's actions |
| own up to (something) | to admit honestly that one has done something wrong |
| make amends | to take action to correct a wrong one has done |
| deflect blame | to redirect responsibility for a fault onto someone or something else |
| a scapegoat | a person unfairly blamed for the wrongdoing of others |
| save face | to avoid humiliation or preserve one's dignity, especially after a mistake |
| damage control | actions taken to limit harm to one's reputation after a mistake or scandal |
| ring hollow | to sound insincere or unconvincing, despite the words used |
| ring true | to sound genuine and convincing |
| come clean | to admit the truth about something, especially after concealing it |
| accountability theater | visible but ultimately hollow gestures of responsibility, performed for appearances rather than genuine change |
| contrition /kənˈtrɪʃ.ən/ | sincere remorse or guilt for having done wrong |
| too little, too late | said of an action or apology that comes after the damage is already done, diminishing its value |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Strategic Passive vs. Sincere Active Voice**

Voice is a moral choice. An agentless passive construction can quietly erase the wrongdoer from the sentence, while a deliberately chosen active voice puts them squarely back into it.

Three patterns:

1. **Agentless passive for evasion** — removing the subject entirely so no one is grammatically responsible.
   - *Mistakes were made. Lessons will be learned.*
2. **Sincere active voice for accountability** — naming the subject directly as the one who acted and who now answers for it.
   - *I made the mistake. I take full responsibility for it.*
3. **Mixed register shift exposing both** — moving from passive evasion into active ownership within the same passage, exposing the contrast.
   - *It is regretted that certain decisions led to this outcome. No — I made those decisions, and I own them.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Device | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Reported speech with nuanced distancing (it would appear that, is alleged to have, ostensibly) | Lets a REPORTER attribute someone else's claim without endorsing it — epistemic caution about another person's statement |
| C2 (Day 20) | Strategic passive vs. sincere active voice (mistakes were made vs. I made the mistake) | Exposes how the WRONGDOER THEMSELVES uses grammar to evade or accept responsibility — voice choice as moral exposure, not epistemic caution |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Public apologies, corporate crisis statements, political accountability speeches, personal apologies after conflict, media analysis of non-apologies — any context where the grammar of a statement reveals whether responsibility is being owned or dodged.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a public apology statement — real, fictional, or for a public figure of your invention — that starts as a non-apology and then shifts into genuine accountability. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate shift from agentless passive to sincere active voice.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one sentence per word about apologies, accountability, or spin.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. What's the worst non-apology you've ever heard — from a public figure, a brand, or even someone you know personally?
2. How can you tell, in the moment, whether an apology rings true or rings hollow?
3. Give me a real "mistakes were made" sentence, then rewrite it right now as a sincere, fully accountable active-voice apology.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 19 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah pergeseran passive-ke-active yang dipakai user benar-benar mengekspos pilihan moral, atau hanya pergantian tata bahasa tanpa efek retoris + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu pergeseran voice baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *notwithstanding, in light of* / native: *fair enough, having said that*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing public apologies (e.g. **damage control**, **ring hollow**, **accountability theater**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the exposure of sincerity or spin — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| The company say sorry but they don't really explain what happen or who is fault. | The company's statement was a textbook non-apology — vague, agentless, and carefully worded to avoid naming who was actually responsible. | Naming the exact craft term ("non-apology") and the grammatical evasion does the analytical work the vague original cannot. |
| He said sorry many time but I don't believe him because it sound fake. | His apology rang hollow — repetition without contrition rarely convinces anyone. | "Rang hollow" and "contrition" name precisely what "sound fake" only gestures at. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, dan sedikit skeptis-analitis — topik ini secara alami mengundang nada seorang pengamat yang jeli membaca spin, tanpa kehilangan kehangatan saat mengoreksi.
- Error umum di topik ini: tetap menggunakan passive evasif sepanjang tulisan tanpa pernah benar-benar beralih ke active voice yang accountable; mencampur "take responsibility" dengan tindakan nyata yang tidak pernah disebutkan (klaim kosong); kehilangan kontras karena non-apology dan apology asli ditulis dengan nada yang sama datar.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft voice-shift — contoh: "That shift — from 'mistakes were made' to 'I made the mistake' — is exactly the kind of grammatical accountability this topic rewards."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mengambil satu non-apology nyata yang pernah mereka dengar (publik figure, brand, atau pribadi), lalu menulis ulang versi yang benar-benar accountable kalimat demi kalimat — latihan rewrite ini melatih insting mendeteksi spin jauh lebih cepat daripada teori.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Now strip out every passive construction from that apology — does it still sound sincere, or does it suddenly sound worse?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

### DAY 21 — Folklore, Proverbs & Inherited Wisdom Across Cultures

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| a proverb | a short, traditional saying that expresses a commonly held piece of wisdom |
| an old wives' tale | a traditional, often unscientific belief passed on informally, especially among older generations |
| a parable | a short story designed to illustrate a moral or spiritual lesson |
| folklore | the traditional beliefs, stories, and customs of a community, passed down orally |
| oral tradition | the practice of passing stories, beliefs, and knowledge from generation to generation by speech alone |
| a maxim | a short, memorable statement expressing a general truth or rule of conduct |
| an adage /ˈæd.ɪdʒ/ | a saying that is widely accepted as true through long use |
| a fable | a short tale, often featuring animals, that teaches a clear moral lesson |
| the moral of the story | the lesson about right behavior that a story is intended to teach |
| inherited wisdom | knowledge or guidance passed down from earlier generations |
| conventional wisdom | the generally accepted belief or opinion about something, not always accurate |
| a folk belief | a traditional belief held by ordinary people, often without scientific basis |
| superstition | a belief or practice based on fear of the unknown rather than reason or evidence |
| timeless wisdom | guidance or insight that remains relevant and true across generations |
| archaic /ɑːˈkeɪ.ɪk/ | belonging to an earlier period; no longer in ordinary use |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Idiomatic Proverb Structures & Archaic Fixed Forms**

Proverbs don't follow ordinary modern syntax — they survive in fixed, often archaic grammatical molds. The fossilized structure itself signals tradition and lends the saying its authority.

Three patterns:

1. **"He who..." archaic relative construction** — an old-fashioned relative clause opening, rarely used outside proverbs today.
   - *He who laughs last, laughs longest.*
2. **Elliptical imperative-comparative proverb form** — a clipped, balanced structure omitting connecting words for rhythmic memorability.
   - *Waste not, want not. More haste, less speed.*
3. **Inverted comparative structure for proverb emphasis** — reversing normal word order to heighten the proverb's rhythmic and rhetorical weight.
   - *The bigger they are, the harder they fall.*

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Structure | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| C1 | Consistently modern, formal/academic syntax within contemporary Standard English grammar | Builds authority through PRECISION and explicit logical structure |
| C2 (Day 21) | Archaic fixed proverb structures ("he who...", elliptical imperatives, inverted comparatives) | Builds authority through AGE and TRADITION itself — the fossilized grammar IS the source of the saying's persuasive weight |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Storytelling across cultures, grandparents' advice, motivational speeches drawing on tradition, comparative folklore discussions, writing that deliberately invokes the weight of inherited wisdom — any context where an old, fixed form carries more authority than a modern paraphrase ever could.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a short reflection comparing a proverb or piece of folklore from your own culture with one from another culture — what wisdom do they share, and where do they diverge? Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least one deliberate archaic or inverted proverb structure.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one sentence per word reflecting on folklore, proverbs, or inherited wisdom.

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. What's a proverb or piece of folk wisdom from your own family or culture that you still believe, even if you can't fully explain why?
2. Is there an old wives' tale you grew up hearing that you now know is scientifically false — but still find yourself half-believing?
3. Invent your own proverb right now, using one of the archaic structures we just covered — go.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 20 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: apakah struktur arkais/proverb yang dipakai user benar-benar terasa fossilized dan berwibawa, atau hanya proverb modern berbalut grammar biasa + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal satu struktur proverb arkais baru, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *as the saying goes, by the same token* / native: *if anything, mind you*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing folklore and proverbs (e.g. **conventional wisdom**, **the moral of the story**, **timeless wisdom**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it sharpens the cultural resonance — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| My grandmother always said a saying that mean if you patient, good thing will happen. | My grandmother's favorite adage was simple: good things come to those who wait. | Naming it as an "adage" and using its natural fixed phrasing carries far more authority than a paraphrased explanation. |
| This old story about animal teach people to not be greedy, it is famous fable. | It's a classic fable — the moral of the story is that greed always costs more than it gains. | "Classic fable" and "the moral of the story" are the precise craft terms; the original merely describes around them. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, dan hangat — topik warisan budaya secara alami mengundang nada yang lebih personal dan menghargai tradisi, tanpa kehilangan ketajaman koreksi.
- Error umum di topik ini: menulis proverb dengan grammar modern biasa sehingga kehilangan bobot arkaisnya; mencampur "folklore" dengan "history" seolah sama (folklore tidak harus faktual); the moral of the story dinyatakan terlalu eksplisit di awal alih-alih dibiarkan muncul dari ceritanya sendiri.
- Template pujian: spesifik ke craft arkais — contoh: "'He who hesitates is lost' — that archaic relative clause is doing real rhetorical work; a modern paraphrase would never land with the same authority."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mengambil satu nasihat modern yang biasa mereka dengar, lalu menulis ulang dalam bentuk proverb arkais (he who..., waste not want not, the bigger...the harder) — latihan transformasi ini melatih insting fixed-form jauh lebih cepat daripada teori.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Now say that same piece of wisdom again, but this time, give it the 'he who...' treatment."
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas.

#### 6. 🔗 PROMPT — Day 21 (Copy-Paste ke ChatGPT)

```
Topik: Folklore, Proverbs & Inherited Wisdom Across Cultures
Panggil aku [PANGGILAN] [NAMA].
Level bahasa Inggrisku: C2 (Mastery/Proficient).
Kamu Kak Ara, personal AI Coach kamu, dari Inggrisin Yuk. Tugasmu membimbingku belajar vocab lewat writing dan speaking di Level C2 (Mastery).

Gaya bahasa: sopan, ramah, humble (rendah hati — tidak menggurui), tapi singkat, langsung, dan native-like — anggap aku sudah fasih, jangan jelaskan ulang teori dasar grammar.
Gunakan Full English untuk SEMUA penjelasan, instruksi, koreksi, dan feedback — TANPA terjemahan atau catatan Bahasa Indonesia dalam bentuk apapun, termasuk di tabel Box of Words (tidak ada kolom Bahasa Indonesia sama sekali).
Koreksi dibuat SINGKAT dan TAJAM — satu kalimat per error, gaya native menegur native.
Tampilkan phonetic symbol UK setelah setiap kosakata dalam tanda / /.

LANGKAH 1 — Sapa santai dalam English, sebutkan ini Day 21 dan singgung sekilas topik Day 20 (The Art of the Apology) sebagai vocab refresh sebelum lanjut ke topik baru. Lalu langsung tampilkan:
📦 Box of Words — Use EXACTLY these 15 words (do not add or substitute any):
a proverb, an old wives' tale, a parable, folklore, oral tradition, a maxim, an adage, a fable, the moral of the story, inherited wisdom, conventional wisdom, a folk belief, superstition, timeless wisdom, archaic
Display in a 2-column table only: Kosakata+phonetic | English Definition. Add UK phonetics where not shown.
✍️ Writing Challenge — Mode Cerita (8-10 kalimat membandingkan proverb/folklore dari budaya sendiri dengan budaya lain, pakai 5 kata BOW + minimal 1 struktur proverb arkais atau inverted) dan Mode Kilat (5 kalimat, 1 per kata BOW, reflektif tentang folklore/proverbs/inherited wisdom).
Grammar fokus hari ini: Idiomatic Proverb Structures & Archaic Fixed Forms — jelaskan singkat kenapa ini beda dari syntax modern formal/akademik C1 yang konsisten: di Day 21, otoritas dibangun lewat USIA dan TRADISI itu sendiri — struktur arkais yang fossilized ("he who...", elliptical imperative, inverted comparative) justru MENJADI sumber bobot persuasif proverb, bukan presisi logis modern.

LANGKAH 2 — Setelah aku kirim tulisan, kalau ada SATU pola error paling signifikan (terutama soal proverb yang ditulis dengan grammar modern biasa sehingga kehilangan bobot arkaisnya, atau moral of the story yang dinyatakan terlalu eksplisit), tandai dulu HANYA lokasi + jenis errornya dalam satu kalimat tajam tanpa kasih jawaban (Self-Check Pertama), tunggu responsku. Kalau tulisanku sudah ≥95% benar, lewati langsung. Lalu jalankan Koreksi 8 Langkah: (1) Koreksi Writing (tabel Kalimat Asli | Kalimat Benar | Why singkat, tanpa kolom Bahasa Indonesia), (2) Analisa BOW + sertakan 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 20 (vocab refresh), (3) Analisa CEFR (saran mempertahankan Mastery), (4) 5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph, (5) Discourse Markers, (6) Craft & Lexical Chunks — 2-3 lexical chunks native speakers use discussing folklore/proverbs (e.g. **conventional wisdom**, **the moral of the story**, **timeless wisdom**); check if used naturally (✅); suggest one, (7) Register/Formality Check — Spot any register slippage (formal/colloquial, academic/journalistic, or pragmatic tone mismatch). Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent, (8) Speaking Challenge (3 pertanyaan tentang family proverbs, old wives' tales, dan inventing a proverb). If my writing is blank or not in English, ask me to write first.

LANGKAH 3 — Kalau aku aktifkan mode suara dan ketik "Let's start speaking!", ajukan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, koreksi singkat dan langsung.
```


---

### DAY 22 — 🌉 Climate Grief & the Language of Loss

> 🌉 **Bridge Day:** This topic overlaps with B1 (Environment Day), B2 Day 22 (Climate Policy & International Agreements), and C1 Day 22 (Climate Justice & Intersectionality) — but the reframe is total. Where B1 built the vocabulary of environmental concern, B2 examined the politics of climate agreements, and C1 explored the ethics of who bears the burden of climate change, C2 reaches the deepest, most personal layer: the language of grief for what is already being lost — solastalgia, anticipatory grief, the elegy for a glacier. These questions can only be carried with the full rhetorical and grammatical toolkit built from Day 11 to Day 21.

#### 1. 📚 Detail Materi

**Box of Words (15 kata):**

| Kosakata | English Definition |
|---|---|
| solastalgia /ˌsɒl.əˈstæl.dʒə/ | the distress caused by environmental change to one's home landscape |
| ecological grief | grief experienced in response to the loss of ecosystems, species, or landscapes |
| eco-anxiety | chronic fear or dread of environmental catastrophe |
| a vanishing landscape | a landscape undergoing visible, ongoing change or disappearance |
| bear witness (to loss) | to be present and acknowledge a loss, especially as a form of testimony |
| grieve for (a place/species) | to feel deep sorrow over the loss of a place or living thing |
| an extinction event | an occurrence in which a species, or many species, die out completely |
| a ghost forest | a stand of dead trees, often killed by saltwater intrusion or climate-driven change |
| mourn (the loss of) | to feel and express sorrow over a loss |
| an elegy for (a place/species) | a mournful piece of writing lamenting the loss of something |
| the last of its kind | the only remaining example of a species or thing |
| a slow-motion disaster | a catastrophe that unfolds gradually rather than suddenly |
| a tipping point | a critical threshold beyond which a system shifts into a dramatically different state |
| anticipatory grief | grief felt in advance of a loss that has not yet fully happened |
| a changed world | a world permanently altered by loss or upheaval |

**Grammar/Rhetorical Device: Mixed Grammar/Device Combo**

From Day 11 to Day 21, each session isolated a single device. At Mastery level, the language of grief, loss, and moral weight cannot be carried by one device alone — it demands every tool at once. This bridge Day is where all eleven devices from Day 11 through Day 21 can be drawn on simultaneously.

Eleven devices in action — all through the lens of climate grief:

1. *What do we mourn when we mourn a glacier — the ice, or the futures it would have kept cool?* — **rhetorical question & antithesis** (Day 11)
2. *"Ecosystem services have been severely degraded." What that means is: the reef is gone.* — **register-shifting fluency** (Day 12)
3. *The Amazon, once a lung exhaling the breath of millions, now chokes on its own smoke.* — **apposition & embedded aside** (Day 13)
4. *Scientists call it "ecological succession." The rest of us call it watching the forest disappear.* — **comparative register awareness** (Day 14)
5. *A ghost forest. Miles of it. Then—* — **advanced ellipsis** (Day 15)
6. *It was not alarmism. It was prophecy.* — **fragment punchline** (Day 16)
7. *The coral bleaches, the seasons shift, the rivers recede — and the last old-growth tree falls without a sound.* — **cumulative sentences & climactic ordering** (Day 17)
8. *We ought to have listened when the data first came in. We cannot now say we weren't warned.* — **modal nuance for moral stance** (Day 18)
9. *Empty reef. Warmer water. 2050.* — **compression & implication** (Day 19)
10. *It is regretted that certain thresholds have been exceeded. — We crossed those thresholds. We chose this.* — **strategic passive vs. sincere active voice** (Day 20)
11. *He who inherits the earth also inherits the debt that was left in it.* — **archaic proverb structure** (Day 21)

**Kontras fungsi (bukan sekadar tingkat kesulitan):**

| Level | Device Scope | Fungsi |
|---|---|---|
| Day 11–21 (C2) | One primary grammar/rhetorical device per session | Builds individual mastery of a single craft tool at a time |
| Day 22 (Bridge) | Mixed combo — all 11 devices available at once | Tests fluency at the emotional edge: grief and loss demand every device simultaneously, not one at a time |

**Konteks penggunaan:** Climate journalism, ecological elegy, personal essays on environmental loss, grief writing, public speeches on biodiversity — any context where the full weight of irreplaceable loss must be carried through language.

---

#### 2. ✅ Detail Task

**Writing Challenge**

📖 **Mode Cerita** (8-10 kalimat): Write a short piece on ecological loss or climate grief — a place you've loved and watched change, a species you associate with childhood, a landscape you fear for. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and deliberately combine at least THREE different devices from Days 11-21.

⚡ **Mode Kilat** (5 kalimat): Pick 5 words from the Box of Words. Write one sentence per word, each using a different device from the C2 toolkit (Day 11-21).

**Speaking Challenge** (3 pertanyaan, ditampilkan setelah koreksi writing):
1. Is there a place — a landscape, a season, an animal — you've already started to grieve, even while it still exists?
2. What's the difference, for you personally, between eco-anxiety and ecological grief?
3. Write me a one-sentence elegy for something the world has already lost — make it land.

---

#### 3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah

1️⃣ **Koreksi Writing** — Tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (satu kalimat tajam). Kalimat sudah tepat ditandai ✅, Why diisi "—".

2️⃣ **Analisa BOW** — Cek setiap kata BOW yang dipakai user: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural pengganti, ringkas, langsung. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 21 (vocab refresh).

3️⃣ **Analisa CEFR** — Evaluasi singkat: berapa banyak device dari Day 11-21 yang benar-benar berhasil dikombinasikan secara natural dalam tulisan user (sebutkan device mana yang teridentifikasi) + 1-2 saran mempertahankan Mastery.

4️⃣ **5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph** — Tabel ringkas What/Why/Where/When/Who/How dari tulisan user, lalu "Enriched Paragraph" versi yang sama dengan tambahan minimal dua device baru yang belum dipakai user, full English.

5️⃣ **Discourse Markers** — Cek pemakaian. Kalau belum ada, sarankan 2-3 (akademik: *by the same token, notwithstanding* / native: *then again, if anything*) + contoh kalimat.

6️⃣ **Craft & Lexical Chunks** — 2–3 lexical chunks native Mastery-level speakers use discussing ecological loss (e.g. **bear witness to loss**, **a slow-motion disaster**, **the last of its kind**). Identify any in user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one with a single sharp note on why it deepens the grief register — one sentence, no over-explanation.

7️⃣ **Register/Formality Check** — Spot any unintentional register slippage versus deliberate, controlled register-shifting for emotional effect. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (one sharp native-to-native note). ✅ skip if consistent throughout.

8️⃣ **Speaking Challenge** — tampilkan 3 pertanyaan di atas.

**Contoh koreksi (ilustrasi gaya, bukan template kaku):**

| Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why |
|---|---|---|
| I feel very sad because the environment is changing and many animals are gone. | The solastalgia is real — not for a distant catastrophe, but for a changed world I can see from my own window. | "Solastalgia" and "a changed world" locate the grief precisely; the original only states it. |
| The government say sorry but still don't do enough to stop this disaster. | It is regretted that targets were missed — but we chose to miss them. That distinction matters. | The shift from agentless passive to sincere active voice exposes exactly what the original flat statement only implies. |

---

#### 4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

- Tone: native-direct, ringkas, dan dalam — topik duka ekologis mengundang nada yang paling personal dan paling berat sepanjang C2, feedback boleh mencerminkan keseriusan itu tanpa drama berlebihan.
- Error umum di topik ini: mendeskripsikan perubahan iklim secara statistik atau political alih-alih melalui lens personal/emosional; hanya memakai satu device (biasanya modal nuance saja) padahal tujuan Day ini adalah kombinasi; kehilangan kekhususan — "nature is dying" adalah pernyataan abstrak, bukan duka ekologis yang nyata.
- Template pujian: spesifik dan menyebut device by name — contoh: "That shift from passive evasion to active ownership in the middle — and then the proverb structure at the end — is the kind of range Day 22 was built toward."
- Saran mempertahankan Mastery: dorong user mengambil satu tempat spesifik yang mereka kenal dan sudah berubah, lalu menuliskan ulang perubahannya melalui minimal tiga device berbeda — spesifisitas geografis + kombo device adalah cara tercepat melatih grief register.

---

#### 5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

- Trigger: user mengetik "Let's start speaking!" dengan mode suara aktif.
- Ajukan 3 pertanyaan Speaking Challenge satu per satu, full English, langsung tanpa basa-basi.
- Kalau user lancar: tambahkan pertanyaan lanjutan — misalnya "Can you restate that grief using a proverb structure — 'he who...' or an ellipsis that breaks off exactly where the loss becomes unspeakable?"
- Kalau user macet: beri paraphrase singkat atau pilihan jawaban, full English, tanpa penjelasan panjang.
- Pujian hanya di akhir sesi, tulus dan ringkas — boleh menyinggung sekilas perjalanan dari Day 11 sampai Day 22.

---
